Yu Qiaqing and Others Submit a Request to the Zhejiang Provincial Government to Transfer the Administration of Shengsi Islands to Zhejiang; Approved by the Military Commission Last Winter 100

Nantong Fishery Association and Others Publish Opposition in Newspapers

Shenshi News Agency reports that the issue of transferring the administration of Shengsi Islands, which belong to Chongming County, to Zhejiang was approved by the Military Commission in November of last year after being submitted by the Zhejiang Provincial Government, but has not yet been formally implemented. Unexpectedly, recently, the Township and Baojia Chiefs of the islands, as well as the Fishery Associations and Aquatic Products Associations of Nantong and other twelve counties, published their opposition in newspapers. Yu Qiaqing and other chairmen of the Ningbo, Dinghai, and Fenghua Fellow-Provincials Associations in this city have specially drafted a memorandum and submitted it to Huang Shaoxiong, Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, requesting him to uphold justice and promptly transfer the administration. The memorandum outlining the actual situation of why Shengsi Islands should be under the jurisdiction of Zhejiang is as follows: "We respectfully submit this memorandum to your review, as in December of last year, your government received a letter from the Third Department of the Office of the Military Commission, stating that the Chairman had forwarded a report from Zhao Juesheng, Administrative Inspector of the Ningbo Administrative Inspectorate District in Zhejiang Province, requesting that the Shengsi Islands, which belong to Chongming County, be placed under the administration of Zhejiang. This was approved and ordered to be implemented, and a copy of the original report was sent to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for their reference and implementation. The fishermen on the islands were overjoyed upon hearing the news. Recently, we read in the newspapers that more than 200 Township and Baojia Chiefs from various islands in Shengsi, as well as 31 Fishery Associations and Aquatic Products Academic Organizations from Nantong and other places, published their opposition, especially Lu Yanghao, who claimed to be from Jiangsu, and his memorial to the Civil Affairs Department, which was most forceful. To correct this distortion of facts and confusion of public opinion, we dare to refute it item by item as follows. Lu Yanghao's memorial (hereinafter referred to as Lu's memorial)

Based on the Kangxi

The tablet erected on Xiaoyangshan in the 29th year, Lu's memorial claims that the most powerful evidence for not transferring the islands to Zhejiang is the Xiaoyangshan tablet. However, geographical evolution has never been fixed. For example, Shengsi's belonging to Jiangsu only began during the Qing Dynasty. If we trace it back to the Ming, Yuan, and Song Dynasties, the islands belonged to Zhenhai, as clearly recorded in the Zhejiang Tongzhi and various old county records. Comparing this to that, it can be seen that the tablet erected by the government during the Kangxi period cannot be regarded as immutable. With the establishment of the Republic and the renewal of all government affairs, changes in systems and calendars, as well as transfers of provinces, prefectures, and counties, have been countless. Why should this tablet be regarded as sacred and inviolable? Regarding Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Industrial Plan, 'Along the coasts of the eastern Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Fujian provinces, six fishing ports should be built. Six, Xinyang Port in eastern Jiangsu. Seven, Lvsi Port north of the mouth of the Yangtze River. Eight, Changtu in the

Zhoushan Islands

center. Nine, Shipu north of Sanmen Port in eastern Zhejiang.' The Shengsi Islands are very close to Changtu Port and fall within the scope of the Changtu fishing port. In comparison, the islands are far from Lvsi Port and have no connection to it. Lu's memorial cites the regulations of the Ministry of Interior regarding the demarcation of provinces, cities, and counties. Firstly, regarding transportation, the islands are more than 120 nautical miles from Chongming and only 100 nautical miles from Dinghai. A portion of the islands is separated from Huanglong, which belongs to Dinghai, by only a waterway. If a ship travels between Dinghai and the islands, it can arrive in the evening if it departs in the morning, compared to the four days it takes to travel from Chongming to Shengsi via Shanghai and Ningbo. The convenience or inconvenience is obvious. Moreover, mail has always been routed through Ningbo, further demonstrating the convenience of being under Zhejiang's jurisdiction. Secondly, regarding household registration, private investigations show that the islands have a total of 3,700 households and 16,636 people,

all Zhejiang people,

especially from Ningbo, accounting for almost two-thirds, and from Taizhou, accounting for one-third. There is almost no one from Jiangsu. The customs, habits, and language of the entire island are all Zhejiang. There have never been marriages with people from Chongming. Normally, they do not set foot in Chongming County. The government only has nominal jurisdiction without any local connection. Thirdly, regarding administration, the islands are far from Chongming, and communication is cut off. The residents are subjected to harassment by cunning officials and local bullies, and their grievances cannot be heard. This has led to tragic incidents from time to time. Moreover, residents of the islands who are involved in judicial cases are unfamiliar with the place in Chongming. If they are detained for a case, they need to find a guarantor. However, there is no relative or friend to be found. This difficulty is unavoidable. Fourthly, regarding coastal defense, the islands are often used as a base by pirates. During the late Qing Dynasty, the navies of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces often patrolled here together. After the establishment of the Republic, the joint patrol system was abolished. Whenever there are fishing boats, all

maritime protection

is the responsibility of Zhejiang. Jiangsu has never been involved. Fifthly, regarding bandit suppression, recent incidents of robbery, kidnapping, and looting have occurred frequently, especially Jianhu and Nanbeidingxin on Sijiao Island, which are known to be strongholds of bandits. These places are far from Jiangsu, beyond their reach. The Jiangsu authorities have few patrol ships for suppression and no water police for defense, allowing them to act recklessly and trample on the innocent. The islanders suffer from this scourge and have no way to complain. If the islands can be placed under the jurisdiction of Zhejiang, which can take responsibility for suppressing bandits nearby, the bandit problem can be solved with half the effort. Lu's memorial claims that the association is falsely claiming to represent public opinion. The so-called public opinion has no accurate standard. The islanders live by fishing and most are illiterate. It is impossible to obtain a truly legal expression of public opinion. A check of the real names of the more than 200 Township and Baojia Chiefs will likely reveal that they are fictitious. Moreover, according to reports from the islanders, the Chongming Defense Corps has threatened the Township and Baojia Chiefs, forcing them to sign

sworn opposition

declarations. It is the other side that is falsely claiming to represent public opinion. Lu's memorial uses the island and the dividing line of the river flow as the standard for the border. The island's shape has been drawn and explained in detail in the "Investigation Report" sent by Yue Chang and others, so there is no need to elaborate. As for the so-called Yangtze River and Qiantang River flowing into the sea and merging, the Shengsi Islands are located south and north of the confluence. Those who are slightly familiar with the geography of the outer sea can say this. Based on the above, it is very clear that transferring the islands to Zhejiang is beneficial to Zhejiang and does not harm Jiangsu. In short, the key is that the relationship between the governing and the governed should be based on the trend of facts and the needs of the environment. As for Yao Yongping, director of the Jiangsu Provincial Fishery Farm, who claims in his telegram that transferring the islands to Zhejiang will destroy the Jiangsu fishing industry, this is irrelevant. It should be known that fishermen in the Republic of China have no boundaries. Whether the islands belong to Jiangsu or Zhejiang has no impact on fishing in the two provinces. Moreover,

Jiangsu fishermen

use sand boats, while Zhejiang fishermen use hook boats. Their fishing locations are completely different. The director of the farm is not familiar with the actual situation of the fishing industry, so it is no wonder that he is making up things out of thin air. Furthermore, we have read in the newspapers that local gentlemen such as Han Guojun and Tang Wenzhi have also strongly telegrammed their opposition to the transfer of Shengsi. These gentlemen are local, impartial, and deeply secluded, and have never ventured into the sea. Their names may have been used by others in the telegram, which is unavoidable. We believe that the obstruction in this case must be caused by a few people who are manipulating and disrupting it, prioritizing their personal interests and using local boundaries as a cover. We dare to list the facts and submit them to your review, hoping that you will uphold justice, promptly transfer the administration to alleviate the suffering of the people and resolve the outstanding issue, as it is in the public interest. Respectfully submitted to Huang, Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, by Yu Qiaqing, Chairman of the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai, Liu Hongsheng, Chairman of the Dinghai Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai, and Yu Hualong, Chairman of the Fenghua Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai."

The Ratepayers' Association Sends a Letter to the Municipal Council Requesting the Abolition of the Rickshaw Committee 101

The Public Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association yesterday sent a letter to the Municipal Council stating: "Dear Sirs, We have received a joint letter from ratepayers Wang Jian'e, Ge Futian, Xu Jutang, Cao Zhigong, Liu Zhongying, Chen Jiufeng, Chen Binghui, and others stating that they recently read in the newspaper the abridged version of the Public Concession Municipal Council's budget for this year. Due to the decline of the market, tax revenue has sharply decreased. Therefore, the construction, security, and engineering projects that concern the public in the Concession, as well as the police and fire departments, have been drastically curtailed and personnel have been laid off. For example, the Engineering Department's budget is reduced by 484,100 yuan compared to last year's budget, and up to 18 foreign and Chinese staff members will be laid off by July of this year, saving 67,000 yuan in salaries. The Fire Department has also implemented a reduction in personnel. The five vacancies for station chiefs and deputy station chiefs will not be filled. The previously approved hiring of a secretary has now been suspended. The originally planned hiring of 19 Chinese firefighters, 3 craftsmen, and 1 driver has also been cancelled. Therefore, this year's budget is nearly 30,000 yuan lower than last year. The original budget of 263,420 yuan for storing items has been sharply reduced to 62,130 yuan. The Police Department's budget for this year is 302,970 yuan lower than last year. The source of this reduction is the temporary reduction of police personnel and the retrenchment implemented by the Police Commissioner. For example, the assistant superintendent will not be replaced after his recent retirement, and the number of inspectors, probationary inspectors, Indian constables, and Chinese constables will be reduced by 1, 30, 63, and 58, respectively. In the prison, the number of personnel has been reduced by more than 30 people. The budget for the Volunteer Corps this year is more than 80,000 yuan lower than last year, about one-fifth of the total. This saving comes from clothing repairs, military equipment, and travel expenses. The situation in other departments is also the same. It is clear that the Municipal Council's handling is appropriate and the Financial Secretary is well-versed in finance. However, the Council's temporary Rickshaw Committee, which is a redundant branch of the Police Department's Traffic Division, still requires an annual expenditure of more than 50,000 yuan, with the salaries of the three committee members alone requiring an expenditure of 46,800 yuan. In the midst of the retrenchment in various departments, there is no proposal to abolish or reduce its expenses. This is very surprising, given the Council's previous proposals. The Rickshaw Committee was originally established two years ago to implement the recommendations of the previous Rickshaw Investigation Committee. Since its establishment, what have been its achievements? Ratepayers who are not rickshaw merchants cannot make a judgment. However, the Committee's measures have caused several unprecedented rickshaw crises, which have greatly affected the security of the Concession, such as the conflict between rickshaw pullers and mutual aid societies on August 8, 1934. As a result, the Police Department has not only not reduced the duties of its Traffic Division, but also increased its security responsibilities to prevent the disruption of security due to the crises. Therefore, the Rickshaw Committee's achievements have already affected the security of the Concession, which is a fact that is evident. As ratepayers in the Public Concession, we should all admire the Municipal Council's retrenchment to avoid increasing the burden on ratepayers. However, it is very regrettable that the temporary Rickshaw Committee, which was established for a trial period of only eight months, has not been abolished after a year and that its budget has not been reduced. It is clear that its retrenchment standards do not distinguish between urgent and non-urgent matters. If the Rickshaw Committee is needed for consultation in addition to the Police Department's enforcement and management due to the complexity of the rickshaw issue, the Municipal Council already has a Rickshaw Special Committee. It is only necessary to enrich the organization of the Special Committee, or to follow the example of the Singapore Rickshaw Committee, where the committee members are honorary and do not require any expenses. If the Rickshaw Committee is not abolished because it was established for certain individuals and must exist permanently, then there are many other businesses in the Concession that require licenses, such as taxi companies, bus companies, tram companies, hotels, theaters, restaurants, teahouses, bathhouses, dance halls, and brothels. These could all have redundant branches established for them. The impact of this would not only waste the ratepayers' blood and sweat but also destroy the Council's good administrative system. Therefore, the Municipal Council should abolish the redundant Rickshaw Committee during the retrenchment, which would not only save more than 50,000 yuan per year but also reduce crises in the Concession to improve security. We respectfully request that the Council inform the Municipal Council and the Chinese Directors to follow the will of the ratepayers and abolish the Rickshaw Committee in a timely manner during this period of retrenchment to demonstrate proper savings and balance the budgets of various departments to maintain the security and order of the Concession."

Two US Government Offices to Relocate 103

Dalu News reports that according to the US Consulate General in Shanghai, the Consulate General and the US Court for China will relocate from the old Kerry Hotel building at the corner of Jiujiang Road and Jiangxi Road to a new building at the corner of Jiangxi Road and Fuzhou Road on or around March 26. They have leased the fourth, fifth, sixth, and seventh floors of the building. The US Court for China will move in a day or two before the Consulate General, as the Court has 8,000 books and archives, and the Consulate General has about the same number. If they move at the same time, it will be easy to confuse them and difficult to sort them out. The final preparations for the relocation will be made once the bookshelves in the new building are completed.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Instructs that Scrip Should Be Stamped 107

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce replied yesterday to the Yantai Jufeng Bank's Zhongzhuang, instructing that scrip should be stamped according to law. "On the 13th of this month, we received your letter inquiring whether scrip can be considered a type of check and thus be exempt from stamping. We stated that this matter required detailed study before a reply could be given. Now, after examining Article 16, Section 4 of the revised Stamp Tax Law, in the remarks column, checks and scrip are listed separately and are not considered the same type. Furthermore, the tax exemption column only states that checks are temporarily exempt from stamping, so the scope of exemption cannot be extended to scrip by analogy. This letter is sent accordingly, and we hope you will investigate and act accordingly."

The Central Savings Society Confirmed Reorganization; The Sino-French Savings Society's Various Measures 114

The Central Trust Bureau, after receiving an order from the Ministry of Finance to take over the Sino-French Savings Society, established the Central Savings Society to continue operations. The society has now completed preparations and is scheduled to open on the 16th of this month. Specific measures have also been formulated for the reorganization of the Sino-French Savings Society's various savings plans and have been notified to the depositors. It is reported that the Sino-French Savings Society's lottery savings certificates can be exchanged for new certificates from the Central Savings Society without any loss. As for special installment savings, the society, in order to benefit the depositors, will allow the exchange of new certificates at the original full amount of the lottery savings. Ordinary savings from the Sino-French Savings Society that have matured can be withdrawn in cash from the society or continued to be deposited with the Central Trust Bureau. Those that have not yet matured will be deposited with the Central Trust Bureau, and interest will be paid in accordance with the savings regulations. It is also reported that the Central Savings Society, in order to ensure careful handling, will centralize all exchange procedures at its headquarters at 126 Hankou Road in Shanghai. However, after the exchange, depositors can contact branch societies in various locations to make payments, in order to facilitate convenience, as the society will soon establish branch societies and agencies throughout the country.

Currency Expert Geng Aida Gave a Lecture at the Shanghai Business College Yesterday, Entitled "The Evolution of Chinese Currency" 117

Currency expert E. Kann gave a lecture at the invitation of the National Shanghai Business College yesterday. The title of the lecture was "The Evolution of Chinese Currency." The lecture began after an introduction by the school's Dean of Academic Affairs, Gan Shaode. Mr. Geng first described the use of shells, knives, and cloth as currency in prehistoric times, then described the adoption of precious metal currency and the development of the bill system in the Song Dynasty (flying tickets), the Yuan Dynasty's management of currency, and the reasons for its failure. Finally, he explained China's recent monetary policy, such as the abolition of taels and the introduction of the yuan in 1933, the collection of the silver export equalization tax in 1934, and the new monetary policy in November 1935. He expressed admiration for all the reforms of China's currency system and earnestly hoped that the Chinese people would believe in the various new measures.

It is also reported that the Department of Business Administration, in view of the economic downturn in society, has organized a research class in business administration to conduct in-depth research and to subsidize the investigation and study of the actual situation of Chinese industry and commerce. Starting this semester, they will visit well-managed companies and factories every week. They also schedule industrial and commercial management experts to give lectures at the college every week. Last week (February 4), Mr. Tian Bingwu was invited to speak on "Principles and Practices of Personnel Management." This week (March 13), Dr. He Qingru, the president of the Personnel Management Association, was invited to speak on "Problems of Implementing Scientific Management in Chinese Industrial and Commercial Circles." Dr. He gave a detailed and insightful explanation of the reasons why the implementation of scientific management in Chinese industrial and commercial circles has not been successful, and he also described the various problems that China currently urgently needs to improve in management, as well as the solutions to them. The audience was very enthusiastic.

The Case of a Counterfeiting Operation Discovered on Haichang Road: All Six Defendants Confessed 118

According to the Guowen News Agency, the captain of the Detective Brigade of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, Ji Yuanpu, received a tip that there was a counterfeiting operation at 502 Haichang Road. He ordered the squad leader of the brigade, Qiu Yifan, and detectives Tong Wenduan, Zhu Lie, Ge Yifei, Lu Caigao, and Guan Hensheng, to go to 520 Haichang Road on the afternoon of the 12th of this month in conjunction with the Fourth District Branch. They arrested six counterfeiters and seized evidence, including 128 counterfeit two-jiao coins, 13 counterfeit five-jiao Central Bank auxiliary coins, one counterfeit three-jiao five-fen Central Bank auxiliary coin, four genuine one-yuan bills, five jiao five-fen genuine auxiliary coins, nine genuine two-jiao coins, six seals, three boxes of ink, and seven pawn tickets. After the arrest, they were taken back to the brigade for interrogation. According to their confessions, Luo Youhua, 62 years old, from Hubei, residing at 520 Haichang Road; Chen Fuyuan, 38 years old, from Hubei, residing at 8 Daitou, Yangshupu; Ke Hongen, 22 years old, from Hubei, residing on Ningbo Road; Feng Yonglong, 42 years old, from Hubei, residing at 520 Haichang Road; Luo Chenshi, 60 years old, from Hubei, residing at 520 Haichang Road; and Qin Yushan, 42 years old, from Changzhou, residing at 25 Lane 3, Minxingli, all confessed to manufacturing and selling counterfeit coins.

Qian Yinsheng is Also Accused in the Zhang Jinhai Shooting Death Case; Song Quansheng Admits to Gathering a Crowd to Commit Murder 119

Await the Arrest of Fugitives for Further Verification

Zhang Jinhai, a native of Yangzhou, was a barber at the teahouse opened by Qian Yinsheng in the Niqiangquan area of ​​Pudong. Because the teahouse was located in a remote area, far from the police station, it openly gambled all day long, taking cuts and profiting handsomely. Yang Yusheng (nicknamed "Iron Shop Yusheng"), a gangster, heard about this and went to demand a share. However, the teahouse owner, Qian Yinsheng, refused to yield. Yang was enraged and, feeling he had lost face, gathered Song Quansheng and others on the afternoon of the 16th of last month, each wielding pistols and axes, and stormed the teahouse. Zhang Jinhai was shot in the abdomen and immediately sent to a Shanghai hospital, where he died despite treatment. The body was inspected and identified by Zhang Peiming, a judge from the criminal division of the local court. At the same time, the local police station arrested Song Quansheng and escorted him to the local court for interrogation and prosecution, as reported previously. It is now learned that the deceased's wife, Zhang Liu, stated that her husband's death was caused by the teahouse owner Qian Yinsheng pushing him out the door, leading to him being shot and killed by the gangsters. She filed a lawsuit accusing Qian Yinsheng of causing death by negligence and demanding that he bear corresponding responsibility and be listed as a defendant. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Zhang Peiming presided over the trial in the Twelfth Tribunal. The plaintiff, Zhang Liu, arrived in court with her lawyer, Sun Bawo. The judge ordered the detainee Song Quansheng to be brought to the stand. According to his confession, he was 30 years old, a local, in the sesame oil business, residing in Lujia Ferry, Pudong. The judge asked, "Zhang Jinhai is now dead, are you aware of this?" He replied, "I am not aware." The judge asked, "Qian Yinsheng said that you were wielding an axe that day and injured his left foot, is that true?" He replied, "That is not true. I was collecting debts and passed by the Niqiangquan teahouse. Zhou Heshang, whom I knew, was drinking tea and invited me inside. A fight broke out outside shortly after, and then I heard gunshots. I was terrified and fled home, and I was arrested shortly after. I am truly innocent." The judge asked, "Where does the Zhou Heshang you mentioned live? He lives in Lujia Ferry and runs a small business. I can't find him right now." According to Qian Yinsheng's confession, he was 39 years old, a local, and insisted that Song Quansheng slapped him in the face first and then injured his left foot with an axe. Yang Yusheng fired the pistol, and they were carrying a total of three pistols. The judge asked, "Were there any tea guests named Zhou Heshang?" He replied, "No. Our teahouse is very rural, and only villagers drink tea." At this point, lawyer Sun stated that at the time of the incident, Qian Yinsheng instructed the deceased Zhang Jinhai to peek out the door, and the gangsters had not yet left. Then, Zhang was pushed out, and the gangsters shot him, piercing his abdomen, causing his death. Therefore, Qian Yinsheng is also guilty of negligence and should be listed as a defendant. The judge said, "Zhang Liu cannot file a private prosecution; the prosecutor should be responsible for the litigation." Finally, Zhang Liu stated that she was 30 years old, from Yangzhou, residing in Laobaidu, Pudong, and stated that her husband was pushed out by Qian Yinsheng, otherwise he would not have been injured and killed. She begged for investigation. The judge, based on the confessions, ordered that the other fugitives be arrested for further verification, and the defendants were returned to custody.

Zhang Zuming Accuses Zhou Jinggeng and Others of False Accusation, and Includes a Claim for 50,000 Yuan in Damages 120

The court yesterday reviewed the case where the defendants were denied bail.

Further review pending examination of the records from the three trials.

Zhou Jinggeng, a comprador at Xue Mai Luo Accounting Firm at No. 9 Edward Road in the French Concession, was robbed of a large sum of money in his office on June 9th of the 23rd year [of the Republic], which implicated Zhang Zuming, a Ningbo native and shareholder of Ruichangshun Hardware Store at No. 101 Broadway Road. Zhang then implicated Zhuang Jimin, the owner of both large and small Zhuang Yuan, hardware salesman Wang Lianyou, and Tang Qingyue, the director of Dade Hospital. These individuals were successively arrested, brought before the Second Special District Court for trial, and ultimately found not guilty. The French Police Bureau disagreed and repeatedly appealed to the Higher Third Branch Court and the Supreme Court. The appeals were rejected each time, and the original verdict was upheld. Now, Zhang Zuming, believing that Zhou Jinggeng's false accusation caused him to be wrongfully detained, suffering losses in spirit and reputation, and feeling aggrieved, entrusted lawyer Lu Dingkui to file a criminal self-accusation with the Second Special District Court against Zhou Jinggeng, Gao Yushu, Feng Ti'e, Wan Guirong, Qian Genghua, Wang Guixiang, and others, accusing them of false accusation and perjury, and including a claim for 50,000 yuan in damages. This was reported in the previous newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, the suspects were summoned. The plaintiff Zhang Zuming stated that he was engaged in the hardware business, and in June of the 23rd year [of the Republic], the defendants falsely accused him of being a thief, causing him to suffer damage to his spirit and reputation. When asked who first identified him as a robber, he replied that Gao Yushu first identified him as a robber and reported it to the police. He was arrested by the police at the entrance of Sanshou Lane on Broadway Road. While being taken to the Hongkou Police Station, the defendant Feng Ti'e also came to identify him as a thief. Later, when transferred to the French Police Station, You Guirong and Qian Genghua also identified him as a thief. During the second trial, the defendant Wang Guixiang also identified him as a robber. When asked if Zhou Jinggeng also identified him as a robber, he replied that Zhou Jinggeng also identified him as a thief at the police station. Gao Yushu stated that he worked at Xue Mai Luo Accounting Firm and that a few days after the large sum of money was robbed in June of the previous year, a civilian saw Zhang Zuming passing through the British Concession. He believed that Zhang was indeed the robber at the scene, so he reported it to the police, who dispatched detectives to assist in the arrest. Later, Feng Ti'e also went to the police station to identify him. The owner, Xue Mai Luo, also identified Zhang Zuming as the robber at the police station. Feng Ti'e claimed that he was at the office when the police called at seven o'clock and asked him to go to identify Zhang Zuming as the robber who committed the robbery at the scene. Wan Guirong stated that the detective from the police station called him to the police station, and among more than ten people, he identified Zhang Zuming as the robber. Wang Guixiang stated that the civilian indeed saw Zhang Zuming holding a gun and threatening the boss, Xue Mai Luo. Qian Genghua did not arrive. Zhou Jinggeng stated that he was previously a comprador at Xue Mai Luo Accounting Firm, but he has now resigned and is a comprador at Standard Milk Company. On the day of the robbery, he happened to be out on business and never identified the plaintiff Zhang Zuming as the robber. However, he received a letter from the plaintiff's lawyer on the 20th day of the first month of this year, demanding 32,000 yuan in damages, with a deadline for reply. He presented the letter for inspection and requested that the other four defendants be invited to the court. Lawyer Zhang Shanle defended on his behalf. At this point in the interrogation, Judge Li Changnian instructed that the records from the three trials must be reviewed before setting another date for the hearing. After the instruction, the plaintiff's lawyer, Lu Dingkui, requested the court to grant bail to the defendants, but the judge refused.

Gu Zhuxuan's Smoking Case: Joint Interrogation Yesterday 121

Gu Zhuxuan, who was detained in the outer hospital ward (Guangci Hospital) of the Second Special Court for the case of instigating the assassination of Tang Jiapeng, was discovered to have been involved in two cases: bribing to retract testimony and harboring the smoking of opium. The case of bribing to retract testimony has already been prosecuted by the prosecutor and has been tried once, but the hearing has been postponed. The case of harboring the smoking of opium has also been publicly prosecuted by the prosecutor to the same court. Yesterday morning at 3:00 AM, Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu, along with Prosecutor Wang Ren, arrived at the Second Criminal Court. First, the defendants Jia Furong (42 years old, from Suqian, director of learning guards in the Second Special District Prison, stationed at Guangci Hospital to guard Gu Zhuxuan) and Wu Lu (41 years old, from Yangzhou, director of guards at the Second Special District Detention Center, stationed at Guangci Hospital to guard Gu Zhuxuan) were summoned. Then, Prosecutor Wang rose to make an accusation, stating that the two defendants, Jia Furong and Wu Lu, while performing their duties when stationed at Guangci Hospital, harbored the murderer Gu Zhuxuan, allowing him to smoke opium in the hospital ward. On December 24th of last year, the head of the Second Section, Ouyang Sen, confiscated opium and smoking paraphernalia, as well as white powder cigarettes, etc., from Gu Zhuxuan's prison cell. The two defendants, Jia and Wu, have committed crimes under Article 134 of the Criminal Law and Article 13, Paragraph 3 of the Provisional Regulations on the Prohibition of Opium. The details are stated in the indictment, requesting that they be interrogated according to the law. Jia Furong testified that he has been employed since July of the 22nd year [of the Republic], for two and a half years. When asked if the official had previously heard that the prisoner Li Heshang had reported that he was harboring Gu Zhuxuan's smoking of opium, Jia replied that the two prisoners, Li Heshang and Guo Shanyu, were transferred to the hospital ward one after another last winter. One day, Li Heshang borrowed money from Gu Zhuxuan but failed, and the two quarreled. He learned of this and went inside to mediate. On December 24th, the prisoner Wang A'er dug a hole to escape. He learned of this and reported it to the head of the Second Section. When Wang was taken away for interrogation, Wang confessed that he was stealing opium paste. He then went with the section chief to search and found these dangerous drugs. The opium pipe was found in the toilet. When asked about his duties in the hospital ward, he replied that he was only in charge of preventing prisoners from escaping and fighting. When asked if he went into the hospital room, he replied that he performed his duties at the door. When asked if he inspected the items sent by Gu's family, he replied that there were three parties inspecting: the police, the detention center, and the hospital ward guards. The police station also sent three plainclothes detectives and two patrol officers to monitor. If they discovered opium smoking, they would definitely report it. Wu Lu was then summoned and testified that the hospital ward was managed by the prison. Due to the great responsibility after Gu Zhuxuan was detained last year, the prison requested the detention center to send him to guard. When asked if he inspected the items sent by Gu's family, he replied that only the hospital staff inspected them first, and then he and others inspected them again. The prisoner Li Heshang testified that he was convicted of life imprisonment for robbery and murder and was transferred to the outer hospital ward on January 27th of last year due to illness. One night, late at night, Gu Zhuxuan was making noise, and he intervened, asking him to be quieter, but Gu scolded him. At that time, Gu was smoking opium in the room, and prisoner No. 963 was preparing the opium for him. He reported this to Director Jia, but Jia said that he was not smoking. When asked if Gu Zhuxuan smoked in the morning or at night, he replied that he smoked both morning and night. When asked if he smoked in the small room, he replied yes. When asked if Director Jia said that he was trying to extort Gu, he replied no. At this point, the judge asked Jia Furong, "Li Heshang just said that Gu Zhuxuan was smoking opium and that you were informed of it." Jia replied, "That is not true. He (referring to Li) tried to extort Gu but failed, so I transferred him to the prison. He is therefore holding a grudge." Guo Shanyu, 26 years old, was summoned. He was sentenced to life imprisonment for murder and entered the hospital ward in January of last year due to illness. One night, late at night, Gu Zhuxuan was making a lot of noise. He could not sleep, so he asked him to be quieter, but he refused and argued with him, and reported to Director Jia that they were causing trouble for him. Director Jia said that he would transfer them to the prison tomorrow. When asked if he had said that Director Jia accepted bribes to harbor the act, he replied yes, Gu Zhuxuan smoked opium, and No. 963 prepared the opium for him. Wang A'er was then summoned and testified that he was sentenced for four years and eight months for theft and went to the outer hospital ward in November of last year. One day, due to illness and thirst, he stole a pear from Boss Gu, and Gu saw him and scolded him, saying that he would beat him to death. Therefore, he decided to steal two opium pastes from him. When asked who Gu Zhuxuan asked to buy opium, he replied that Gu Zhuxuan asked Director Wu to buy five yuan of opium every seven days, and Wu stuffed the opium through a hole in the wall. When asked if Director Jia knew that Director Wu bought opium, he replied that Jia saw it but did not care. When asked if the section chief said that he was transferred back to prison because he dug a hole to escape, he replied that it was because he stole opium paste, not to escape. The judge asked Wu Lu, "Wang A'er said that you bought opium for him, is this true?" He replied, "I dare not buy it." Liu Mingjing, from Sichuan, was then interrogated. He was sentenced to five years for theft and entered the hospital ward on November 30th of last year. When asked if he had seen anyone smoking opium, he replied no, but he smelled opium smoke. One day, Gu's maid brought food and told Gu that there was opium in it. Then, Director Jia took the food inside. According to Jia, Liu Mingjing hated him because he scolded him for smoking cigarettes. Chen Guofang, nicknamed "Baidu Bridge," was then interrogated. He was sentenced to nine months for robbery. When asked if he knew about the opium smoking in the small room, he replied that there was no opium smoking. At this point, Li Heshang questioned Chen, saying that Baidu Bridge had personally told him about how Boss Gu smoked opium, how prisoner No. 963 prepared the opium for him, and how Director Jia secretly fitted the key to the small room, but now he denied it. Judge Wang instructed that the case would be adjourned for further interrogation.

Municipal Health Bureau: Crackdown on Private Toilets in the City, Currently Conducting Registration of Private Toilets 123

Those That Are Unnecessary Will Be Eliminated

The Municipal Health Bureau, in view of the proliferation of private toilets in the city, which are detrimental to public health, has received letters from citizens in the district requesting a crackdown. According to Yun Jihua, director of the Shanghai South Health Office of the Health Bureau, the Municipal Health Bureau is currently conducting registration of private toilets. Those that do not meet the requirements of the Health Bureau, or are located on streets where toilets should not be established, will be eliminated. If the Health Bureau believes that there is a need to establish a toilet in a certain location, but there is no public toilet, then temporary permission will be granted for the establishment, to be used as a public toilet, recognizing its property rights. However, private toilets that have been temporarily approved by the Health Bureau must upgrade their facilities, such as installing tap water and electric lights, and connecting to sewers, to improve sanitation. The fee for toilet paper should not be too high, and taxes must be paid to the Finance Bureau. It is learned that there were originally over a hundred private toilets in the city, and as a result of repeated crackdowns by the bureau, the number has gradually decreased, but there are still fifty to sixty today.

Shanghai-Ningbo Line to Collect 20% Liquor Fee Starting the Day After Tomorrow; Thoroughly Eliminate Tea House Extortion 126

The Shanghai-Ningbo line includes China Merchants Bureau's Xin Jiangtian, Ningshao Company's Xin Ningshao, Sanbei Company's Ningxing, Taikoo Company's Xin Beijing, and Daxing Company's Xin Hongxing, five ships. Last year, in order to rectify the tea house's demand for liquor fees and to treat passengers favorably, China Merchants took the lead in implementing the practice. Daxing also planned to temporarily cancel the collection of 20% liquor fee to show uniformity. However, since the trial operation, there have still been instances of passengers and tea houses exchanging liquor fees, and the measures are not thorough enough, which does not align with the original intention of the companies to treat passengers favorably. It is learned that the four companies held a meeting and decided that starting from the 16th of this month (Monday), they would publish a notice stating that all cabin classes would uniformly collect a 20% liquor fee and issue a small ticket, requesting passengers not to give liquor fees again to prevent abuses. Daxing will also publish a notice at the same time to restore the 20% liquor fee collection method. Xin Beijing is still working on the issue of reducing tea houses, and although it has not been listed in the notice at the same time, it will also uniformly charge an additional 10% on passenger tickets starting from the same day to show uniformity.

Shanghai Telephone Bureau Began Oral Examinations for Female Operators Yesterday; Registration and Oral Examinations Continue Today 127

Written Examinations to Be Held Tomorrow

Datong News Agency reports that the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, following instructions from the Ministry of Communications, is conducting recruitment on behalf of the Hankou Telephone Bureau for five official and five alternate female operators without money transfers. Yesterday was the start of registration and oral examinations. More than twenty people went to the bureau's exhibition hall in Dananmen to register. Staff members from the Engineering Department conducted oral examinations in Mandarin, English, and general knowledge. The examinations were completed around 11:00 AM, and only about half of the candidates passed. Examination permits were issued to those who passed.

Examinations Today and Tomorrow

Registration and oral examinations will continue today from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM. Formal written examinations will be held tomorrow, divided into morning and afternoon sessions. Admission to the examinations will be based on the examination permits. The morning examinations will cover Party Principles, Chinese, Arithmetic, and World Geography, from 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM. The afternoon examinations will cover English, Electrical Engineering, General Knowledge, Mandarin, and English, from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM.

Training in Shanghai

The five officially selected candidates who pass the examinations will first receive three months of training at the Shanghai Telephone Bureau, with a monthly stipend of 14 yuan. After the training period, they will be transferred to the Hankou Telephone Bureau to serve, with a starting monthly salary of 30 yuan. The age requirement is from 17 to 23 years old, as youth and vigor are believed to ensure satisfactory service.

Wusong Chamber of Commerce Notifies to Stop Price Reduction Sales 138

Since the war, commerce in the Wusong district has been affected by the economic downturn and rural bankruptcy, leading to a precarious existence. Therefore, various stores have frequently resorted to price reductions. Zhang Yuchi, the director of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce, after receiving instructions from the Social Affairs Bureau to prohibit drastic price reductions by shops, has notified all businesses not to post advertisements with slogans such as "great sacrifice sale," "selling at a loss," or "disregarding costs," or to use improper means to undercut each other, in order to maintain business ethics.

China Postal Worker Special Publication 145

The China Postal Worker Monthly, published by the Propaganda Department of the National Postal Workers' Union of Shanghai, has rich content and insightful arguments and is a rare publication in the cultural world. Therefore, since its publication, it has been popular throughout the country and loved by subscribers. Now, the first volume of the publication has ended, and the combined first, second, and third issues of the second volume were published on the 15th of this month. Because the union is holding its third national congress, this issue is a special publication, with more than three times the usual number of pages. The cover is printed with various stamps, which are exquisite and unique. There are seven pages of photographs, all of which are recent executive and supervisory committee members of postal workers' unions from various places and spectacular views of their exquisite union halls. As for its content, in addition to eight concise and incisive short commentaries, there are articles by Zhu Xuefan on "The Future of the Chinese Labor Movement," by Zhang Liangren on "A Preliminary Discussion of Postal Simplified Life Insurance," by Shui Xiangyun on "The Postal Workers' Movement in Extraordinary Times," by Zhang Zuoqi on "The International Labor Organization and China," and by Xue Ya on "The Necessity and Implementation of the Postal Workers' Economic Construction Movement," all of which are extremely insightful, thorough, and innovative. In addition, the literary column contains thought-provoking short pieces, exquisite new and old poems, and a long novel with bizarre plots, all worth reading. The Postal Knowledge column, which is published continuously in the journal, provides a very detailed description of postal business and postal procedures. For those who are not familiar with postal procedures or who want to study postal science, it is a good reference. Other items, such as postal news and monthly domestic and foreign workers' news, are also extremely useful reference materials. This issue also includes a history of postal workers' unions in various places and an overview of past union activities, providing a detailed description of the origins, development, and current state of the postal workers' movement, making it a valuable material for researchers of the labor movement. The publication is sold by major bookstores and postal workers' unions throughout the country. The annual subscription for twelve issues is one yuan, including postage. Each issue sells for ten cents. This issue is a special issue and sells for twenty cents per copy. The subscription is not increased. Direct subscriptions can be sent directly to the union.

Municipal Council Band to Hold Sunday Concert Tomorrow 147

Tomorrow (Sunday) is the date of the Municipal Council Band's regularly scheduled Sunday concert, the 23rd Sunday concert. The program is popular in nature, and this year marks the 50th anniversary of the death of the great Hungarian writer Franz Liszt. Therefore, the program will consist entirely of Liszt's masterpieces. Liszt was a piano virtuoso, unmatched in ancient and modern times. He was also a famous composer, so those who study Western music history often say that without Liszt and Berlioz (a French writer), Wagner could not have emerged. The creation of orchestral music began with Liszt and Berlioz, and Wagner synthesized their best works to create a spectacular scene. The most widely known of Liszt's compositions are the "Symphonic Poems," a total of thirteen chapters, of which "Tasso" and "Les Préludes" are the most moving. In addition, there are "Hungarian Rhapsodies," etc., all of which will be performed one by one tomorrow. The concert starts at 5:15, and tickets are only one yuan or half a yuan. Music lovers should not miss this opportunity.

Shanghai's Securities Industry (4) 153

— Compiled by China Credit Bureau (Seventeenth Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce)

Handling Fees and Trading Methods: The commission charged by the exchange to brokers is called a handling fee. The standard for collection is calculated based on the actual transaction amount, with 6.25 yuan deducted per 10,000 yuan. Brokers charge their clients double this amount. However, due to varying circumstances among different firms, uniformity is difficult to achieve. Generally, one-thousandth is the common standard, but it has recently dropped to seven or eight ten-thousandths. For bank transactions, some brokers only pay a net spread of 6.25, as the brokers have other considerations.

The actual handling fees collected by the exchange from brokers are required to be partially refunded to the brokers as bonuses at the end of each year, according to the provisions of the business regulations. The method of returning this money depends on the amount of handling fees paid by each broker during the year. Brokers numbered 1 to 55 can receive 2.35 percent, while those numbered 52 to 80 receive only 1.5 percent. This difference is due to the fact that when the goods and securities sections were merged, the 55 brokers who were originally part of the exchange made a request for separate treatment. Therefore, the value of a broker's position varies accordingly. Based on current market value, the former is worth approximately 30,000 yuan, while the latter is worth 25,000 yuan.

The trading method used in the industry is continuous buying and selling. First, brokers solicit transactions from banks, money houses, government agencies, and private clients. Among these, the financial sector accounts for the largest volume, representing one-half of the total. Merchants from the north, merchants from Guangdong, government figures, and capitalists make decisions. During the trading hours specified by the exchange, prices are called out sequentially, and buying and selling are conducted by brokers. Once a counterparty is found, the transaction is declared "completed." After the transaction is completed, the exchange enters it into the floor account, and then both the buying and selling brokers sign the agreement. The exchange also sets an appropriate closing price at the end of each trading day, requiring brokers to settle their accounts accordingly. The profit or loss is settled the next day. Both the buying and selling parties must also pay a special margin deposit of 400 yuan per 10,000 yuan face value. (The amount can be adjusted by the board of directors based on market conditions. Sellers who have physical goods and provide them do not have to pay.) Those who have sufficient funds in their accounts can settle on the delivery date. Otherwise, they must close the position or roll it over before the deadline to end the transaction. This is an overview of the trading method. Other strategies, such as arbitrage (buying near-term contracts and selling far-term contracts to profit from market differences), are not easy to execute without sufficient capital and expertise.

Overview of Brokers: Most brokers at the exchange are financially sound and are organized by financial institutions. Their capital ranges from 30,000 yuan to 300,000 yuan. Successful brokers often have handling fee revenues exceeding 100,000 yuan. A list of the brokers' license numbers and names is provided below: 1. Tong Yi, Li Ziwei; 21. Zhong Yi, Wang Jiaosheng; 3. Shanghai Yuan Da, Yang Yuankai; 11. Chang Ji, Wang Zizhou; 12. Yong Xiang, Zhou Changgeng; 13. Rui Da, Zhu Anfu; 14. Tong Ji, Zhu Bingnian; 15. Jiu Yu, Xia Jindong; 16. Xinhua, Sun Ruihuang; 17. Si Nong, Feng Zhaonan; 18. Jing Feng, Yao Zhenbo; 19. Tong Shang, Gu Changyan; 20. Shun Kang, Ji Guoliang; 21. Shun Feng, Liu Fanwu; 22. Zhen Da Chang, Shi Jiucai; 23. Tai Chang, Ge Qingqi; 24. Hong Kong Football: Hua Lian Wins the Lai Wah Cup; Defeats the Navy League Two to Zero; Feng Jingxiang and Li Huitang Each Score a Goal 157

(Hong Kong Dispatch) The annual Lai Wah Cup football final was held on the 8th at the So Kon Po Stadium between the Hua Lian team and the Navy League team. The weather was mild that day, so football fans flocked to watch the match. Before 4:00 PM, the stadium was already full, and those who arrived later had no place to stand. It is estimated that there were more than 8,000 fans in total. After 90 minutes of hard fighting, Hua Lian defeated the Navy team two to zero, winning this year's championship. In today's match, Hua Lian replaced Huang Meishun with Lin Depu. The center back, Qian Zhujiang, although he did not show any amazing performance, was still able to unite with the backs to defend the city. Depu supervised the opposing center forward, making him unable to do anything. The two backs, Mai Shaohan, were lively and agile, and their coordination was appropriate. It is a pity that the two's heading skills were far inferior to the opponent's, which was a fly in the ointment. In the second half, the Navy League changed its formation, using a fierce kick to attack. The Hua Lian players were helpless, allowing the enemy to penetrate deep into their territory. If it were not for Ji Liang's efforts to defend the dangerous city, Hua Lian would not have been able to keep half of its territory. The performance of the five forwards was far better than the previous day, but their coordination was not yet truly effective. In the first half, they attacked more than they defended, with Feng Jingxiang and Li Huitang scoring two goals in succession. In the second half, the situation changed dramatically. The Navy League turned from defense to attack, and its imposing manner made the spectators breathless. Because the Navy League's forwards were not good at shooting, the Hua Lian defenders, although they were repeatedly surrounded, were still lucky enough to avoid losing. This was Hua Lian's luck, and the Navy League's bad luck. The Navy team used Hu Huachen as the center back. He was more than enough to defend, but still unable to coordinate with the forwards. Moreover, the center forward and the right forward repeatedly missed opportunities, so they were defeated. As for the bravery of the players, it was far beyond what Hua Lian could match.

Outline for the Implementation of Physical Education in Secondary Schools in Jiangsu Province 158

The Ministry of Education has approved the "Outline for the Implementation of Physical Education in Secondary Schools in Jiangsu Province for the 24th Year," submitted by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, and has issued instructions for its filing. The original text of the outline is as follows:

(I) General Principles: All public and private secondary schools in the province must, starting from this year, implement strict physical training for all students in accordance with the provisions of this outline. The ultimate goals of implementing physical training in schools are as follows. Simultaneously or in stages, use practical methods to achieve tangible results: (A) To ensure that the physical fitness of every student is fully developed; (B) To ensure that every student's spirit is lively and resilient; (C) To ensure that every student's physical ability is sufficient to cope with all environments; (D) To ensure that every student's behavior is naturally in accordance with national etiquette and discipline; (E) To ensure that every student's life is full of vigor and vitality. Schools should complete the systematic organization of physical education administration throughout the school within this year to serve as the center for implementing physical training for all students. Schools should establish a physical education budget starting from this year, reducing unnecessary expenses and increasing necessary construction. Schools should formulate concrete plans to expand physical education facilities and equipment starting from this year, implementing them in stages to meet the needs of this outline. Schools should formulate detailed plans and implement them diligently for all physical education activities, including physical education courses, morning exercises, extracurricular activities, and intramural and extramural sports competitions, in accordance with the Ministry's Physical Education Curriculum Standards for Secondary Schools and the provisions of this outline. Schools should conduct rigorous assessments of students' physical training performance starting from this year, and those who fail will not be allowed to advance or graduate. Schools should earnestly conduct physical examinations of students starting from this year, at least once per semester, to serve as the basis for implementing physical training. The implementation of this outline shall be the joint responsibility of the principals, deans, directors of student affairs, business managers, junior high school principals, grade-level teachers, physical education teachers, scout trainers, military instructors, and school doctors of each school. All faculty members of the school have the obligation to assist. The performance of the implementation of this outline shall be subject to rewards and punishments by provincial and county inspectors and special personnel at any time. (II) Administration: Schools should organize a physical education committee to preside over all physical education administration throughout the school. The physical education committee shall be composed of the principal, dean, director of student affairs, business manager, junior high school principal, physical education teachers, scout trainers, military instructors, school doctors, and enthusiastic faculty members. The principal shall appoint one physical education teacher as a standing committee member. The physical education committee shall meet at least three times per semester, and its functions shall be as follows: (A) To determine the annual physical education implementation plan at the beginning of the school year; (B) To compile and review the spending plan and actual spending of physical education funds; (C) To plan the expansion or renovation of sports fields and equipment; (D) To review and approve various management methods for all physical education activities throughout the school; (E) To seek improvements in school hygiene and improvements in student life; (F) Other matters related to the improvement of overall physical education. The standing committee member of the physical education committee shall, under the order of the principal and the entrustment of the physical education committee, plan and implement all physical education matters throughout the school in accordance with the provisions of this outline, and shall compile the implementation situation into a work report and submit it to the physical education committee for review at each meeting. Schools should lead all students to organize various sports groups to achieve the effect of popularization and development. The physical education organizations organized by the students of each school, regardless of the activity, should be subject to the control and guidance of the physical education committee. (III) Funding: Schools should compile a separate spending plan and actual spending for the physical education fees paid by students, the physical education funds in the school budget, and other funds belonging to physical education. At the beginning and end of the school year, the principal shall submit a special report. The physical education funds of each school should be used exclusively for the needs of physical education consumption and equipment and should not be misappropriated arbitrarily. The distribution standard of physical education funds in each school is as follows: (A) Physical education consumption fees, such as the purchase of sports equipment and the repair of equipment, shall not exceed 50% of the total amount; (B) Event fees, such as the expenses of participating in various sports events, shall not exceed 20% of the total amount; (C) Physical education equipment fees, such as the construction of sports grounds and the purchase of fixed equipment, shall not be less than 30% of the total amount. (IV) Equipment: Schools should follow the minimum standards for physical education equipment promulgated by the department, formulate a phased expansion plan together with the budget, and submit them separately for approval. Schools should make full use of the open space in the school to arrange the physical education environment, thereby arousing students' interest and achieving results imperceptibly. Schools should try to make use of the natural environment outside the school to provide students with physical training. Within the possible range, the sports grounds and equipment of each school should be opened to the nearby public for amateur sports, but detailed management methods should be established. Schools should have adequate indoor sports facilities so that students can have adequate activities during rainy and snowy periods. (V) Physical Education Course: The physical education course hours in each secondary school must meet the standards promulgated by the Ministry and must not be reduced. In co-educational schools, girls should take physical education classes separately from boys. If there are too few girls, they may schedule another time and combine classes. As a general rule, physical education classes should not be scheduled within one hour before or after meals and after 4:00 PM each day. When attending physical education class, students should first form a team and wait for the teacher to arrive. The class leader should give the order to stand at attention and salute. The class leader should check the number of students present and absent and the names of the absentees after forming the team and report them clearly to the teacher. When attending physical education class, teachers should pay attention to discipline training to enhance the effectiveness of training and management. When attending physical education class, students should wear uniforms or sportswear. Those who violate this rule will be considered absent without reason. The physical education course should focus on teaching basic sports methods and should not allow students to engage in activities at will according to their preferences. The physical education course should be based on the principle that all students in the class have equal opportunities for activity. If necessary, students may be grouped according to their physical education performance in the previous semester to maintain students' interest in sports. Physical education teachers should prepare a syllabus and details of the physical education curriculum in advance and implement them accordingly. However, the teaching materials for apparatus gymnastics and mat exercises shall be based on the teaching materials promulgated by the department. In addition to adding supplementary teaching materials, all schools should comply. All new students enrolled from the 24th year should be taught as many apparatus gymnastics and mat exercises as listed in the detailed syllabus promulgated by the department. Old students from previous years may make appropriate changes according to their teaching level, but they must still meet the following quantitative standards: (A) In the second and third grades of junior high school, at least 15 kinds of apparatus and mat exercises must be taught each school year; (B) In the second and third grades of high school, at least 10 kinds of apparatus and mat exercises must be taught each school year; (C) Vocational schools may appropriately reduce the number depending on the number of hours. The allocation of types of physical education course materials shall be implemented in accordance with the standards promulgated by the Ministry, but the teaching time for flexibility exercises, apparatus exercises, or mat exercises in each class shall not be less than 20 minutes. The selection of physical education course materials should focus on developing muscle strength and promoting public and private virtues such as courage, decisiveness, cooperation, and sacrifice. Games and entertainment are secondary. Girls may consider using apparatus exercises in the middle school period, and it is especially appropriate to use mat exercises. Dance should focus on fitness and folk dance. Light apparatus exercises may be used in place of flexibility exercises. In the case of girls' physical education classes, each school should have strict regulations and detailed records to maintain physical health and avoid adverse results. However, those who try to avoid this rule must be given a serious warning. In case of heavy rain or wet ground, except for one lesson per month that can be changed to lecturing on physical education knowledge in the classroom, classes should be held as usual in the gym or other places, and should not be suspended on the pretext of weather. Those who do not have indoor sports grounds must change to lecturing on knowledge and sports rules or methods in the classroom. It is permissible to do some indoor exercises or static games. The lecture notes on physical education knowledge should be compiled and printed by the teachers for each student. (The following also includes morning exercises and forced running, etc., which are omitted for brevity.)

Statement by the Pudong Small Ball Association Regarding the Hua Zhi Team Incident 165

To the Editor:

Having read in your esteemed newspaper the other day that the Hua Zhi team, a member of our association, was judged to have violated sportsmanship and received appropriate punishment, it is regrettable that they did not reflect on their actions but instead made careless statements. This not only confuses the public but also undermines the entire small ball (sports) endeavor. It is truly disheartening to speak of. While it is understandable that young people are full of energy and eager to win, for the sake of clarifying the facts, we must correct their statements.

The match in question took place at 9:50 AM on March 1st. The team's claim that it took place on "February 23rd, many weeks ago" is likely due to forgetfulness.

It is common knowledge that the Shi Xin team is not a fundamental team of our association. The only team with fundamental team status is the junior team. This team had a dispute with a friendly team in the youth group, which our association investigated. It was determined that the championship should be awarded to the other team. The team's claim of protecting a fundamental team is self-explanatory.

The match took place on March 1st. The next day, we received a protest letter from the Shi Xin team. After investigation, it was discovered that Wang Degen, who played for the Hua Zhi team on that day, was actually Yao Guanfan. When a meeting was convened, it was unanimously agreed that the use of a completely different name was an undeniable violation of sportsmanship. Therefore, the Hua Zhi team was penalized with a loss, and the player in question was lightly punished with disqualification. This was detailed in the notification sent to the team. However, the team now claims that "the name was not pointed out, clearly fabricating the matter," which shows extreme carelessness.

In conclusion, organizing small ball competitions not only entails enduring hardship and complaints in spirit but also inevitably results in significant material losses. There is absolutely no possibility of seeking personal gain through false pretenses. The Youth Association authorities are dedicated to public welfare and have made sacrifice their sole mission. We have been holding small ball competitions for four sessions. If, as the team claims, we were manipulating championships, who would believe we would do something so unprofitable?

Respectfully,

Pudong Small Ball Association

The City's Boy Scouts Celebrate Children's Day with a Grand Assembly at the City First Sports Field 170

The Boy Scout movement in our country began in the first year of the Republic of China. At that time, as it was still in its early stages, the organization and training were not unified. It was not until March 15th of the 15th year of the Republic of China that the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang decided to place the Boy Scout movement under the leadership of the party and determined its organizational system and training principles. Only then did the Boy Scout movement in our country gradually become perfect. Based on the above historical facts, March 15th is indeed the day when the new life of the Boy Scout movement in our country was officially established, and a grand celebration should be held to commemorate it for a long time. Last year, the General Association of Chinese Boy Scouts convened a training conference, which also resolved that this day should be designated as Boy Scout Day in our country every year. It is now learned that the General Association of Boy Scouts has already formulated commemorative measures and issued them to the Boy Scout organizations in various provinces, cities, and counties, ordering each to hold a celebration ceremony at 8:00 AM tomorrow. The City Boy Scout Council has also decided to comply with the order and hold a celebration assembly at 8:00 AM tomorrow at the City First Sports Field on Daji Road in Nanshi. Each Boy Scout troop in the city has been ordered to send one or two squads of members to attend on time. The order of the celebration ceremony and the list of officers of the assembly are listed below:

Order of Ceremony

Opening of the meeting; Playing music (while setting off firecrackers); Raising the flag; Singing the Party song; Paying the highest respect to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of the Founding Father; Bowing once to the portraits of the Chairman and Vice-Chairman; The Chairman respectfully reads the Founding Father's will; All Boy Scouts recite the Boy Scout Oath; Chairman's report; Speech; Shouting slogans; Singing the Boy Scout song; Playing music; Completion of the ceremony.

Assembly Staff

Presidium: Tong Xingbai, Pan Gongzhan, Leng Xueqiao. Conductors: Sun Yixin, Yu Kuikui, Zhang Xunfang, Sun Hao. Master of Ceremonies: Wu Gang. Recorder: Xie Yanbo. Reporters: Wu Gang, Chen Fenlao. Band: Provincial Shangzhong Troop. Bugle Corps: Guangong Troop. Medical Team: Guangyi Troop.

The Central Research Question for This Session Was Also Decided Yesterday

The Municipal Middle School Normal Education Research Association held its first plenary meeting of this semester at the YMCA of Eight Immortals Bridge at 3:00 PM yesterday to discuss the research results reports of each group from the previous semester and the central research question for this semester. Details are listed below. Attendees included Director Pan of the Municipal Bureau of Education.

Attending Members

Section Chief of the Association, Tong Shiqian, Qian Fugong, Wu Renya, and members Liao Maoru, Zhang Yi, Chen Jicheng, Lin Meiyan, Jia Furu, Yan Zhenchun, Tao Guangchuan, Ma Jiazhen, Wu Zhiqian, Tang Zengyi, Zhang Yifan, Yan Junxuan, Shen Tong, Cao Yuanling, Li Xubin, Zhang Jiashu, Lu Xirong, Ping Hailan, Wu Youxiao, Zhang Shilin, and more than eighty others.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Director Pan, Recorder Qian Fugong. The meeting began with a report by the Chairman, briefly stating that today is the third plenary meeting of the Middle School Normal Education Research Association this semester, to discuss the research reports of each group from the previous semester, and to decide on the central question and research steps for this semester. Due to the excessive number of questions and the early school break last semester, the research association was unable to conclude as scheduled. Currently, the results of all groups, except the Moral Education and Military Training Group, including the results of the Financial Resources and Equipment Group, the Graduation Examination Group, and the Curriculum and Teaching Group, have been submitted for discussion at today's meeting. For the research methods this semester, in addition to the groups that have not yet concluded from the previous semester continuing their research, the other groups intend to change the grouping methods separately. After grouping, the date and location of the small group meetings will be decided by the chairman of each group, and members of each group will be notified, and the Bureau of Education will be notified to send personnel to participate. In addition, regarding the revision of the middle school curriculum standards last year, the Ministry of Education sought opinions, and the association has compiled and submitted them. The revisions announced by the Ministry of Education are completely the same as the results discussed by the association, and have been adopted by the Ministry of Education. It is hoped that in the future, the spirit of the past will be maintained to put forward research on other issues.

Reports from Each Group

Chen Jicheng, Chairman of the Graduation Examination Group, reported that three small group meetings were held last semester, and the various issues were divided into two major categories: graduation examinations and grade assessment. The research results show that the intention of the examination system is very good, but there are many malpractices. Therefore, if it cannot be abolished, two remedial measures have been proposed. Results have also been achieved in the area of grade assessment. Zhang Yi, Chairman of the Financial Resources and Equipment Group, reported that three cases were unresolved last semester, and there were also the results of a separate study by Zhang Du of Maitou Middle School. The Curriculum and Teaching Group Chairman Liao Maoru reported that there were a total of twenty-nine questions last semester, which were discussed in three groups. As the report has not been compiled yet, the meeting minutes of each group will be submitted for discussion.

Discussion Issues

Graduation Examination Group: The first case, the proposal to abolish the graduation examination, was revised to temporarily suspend the middle school graduation examination during the period of preparation for national crisis education and submit the opinion to the Ministry of Education. The remaining cases were passed according to the original proposed results.

Financial Resources and Equipment Group: Except for the third and eighth cases, the remaining cases were passed with modifications according to the original proposed results.

Curriculum and Teaching Group: Except for the sixth case in the first subgroup, the remaining cases were passed with modifications according to the original proposed results.

Curriculum and Teaching Group: Except for the first and sixth cases in the second subgroup, which were reserved for further discussion, and the seventh case, which was canceled, the remaining cases were passed with modifications according to the original proposed results.

Curriculum and Teaching Group: The opinions of the third subgroup on the revision of the normal school curriculum will be reviewed by experts from the Bureau of Education.

This Session's Methods

The central research questions for this session will be divided into two groups: the National Crisis Education Group and the Subject Teaching Method Group. Each school can freely determine which group to participate in and report to the Bureau of Education. The Bureau of Education will then designate the candidates for the chairman of each group.

Finance: Major Speculators Liquidate Long Positions; Standard Gold Price Continues to Decline 177

——Resulting in a Drop of 1.2 Yuan——

Yesterday, due to the approach of the swap period, many major speculators sold off their positions, making it difficult for the gold market to rally at the opening. The March-April spread rose to 3 yuan, and sentiment was weak, leading to a mid-day decline. However, the market managed to close near flat. In the morning, the overseas silver market saw a squeeze over two days, with London rising and the U.S. remaining flat. The Mondelli forward silver price only increased by 1/10 of a cent in March, and the rest remained unchanged. Exchange rates continued to contract. London spot gold rose by a penny. The Central Bank's official exchange rates showed both the British pound and the U.S. dollar remaining flat. The Customs Gold Unit was unchanged. The official standard gold price was raised to 1147.3 yuan. Off-exchange pre-market trading opened at around 48 yuan. Fuxing, Yongda, Decheng, Richang, and Huixiang all sold, causing the price to drop to around 7 yuan. The morning opened lower, and after the opening, the price continued to weaken due to Huixiang's repeated aggressive selling of gold bars. The official HSBC exchange rates showed both the British pound and the U.S. dollar remaining flat. Yingxiang and others maintained support at lower levels, with occasional rallies, but Huixiang's selling appetite was strong. Speculators panicked at one point, but still failed to rally. The silver balancing tax was announced, rising by 1.25 points. After this, there was a slight improvement, but both buyers and sellers were active, resulting in a sideways trend at noon. The afternoon market opened peacefully, but supply exceeded demand, and the market gradually weakened. Speculators rushed to sell, and although major speculators maintained support at lower levels, the report of a 4-anna increase in the Indian silver price fueled the selling sentiment, ultimately leading to a continued decline. However, buying interest was strong after the low, and the market gradually stabilized. Today will mark the start of the April-May swap period. It is predicted that speculators will post offers of 5 yuan and 4 yuan. A record of today's market conditions is as follows:

The morning opening price was 1147.4 yuan, a decrease of 0.7 yuan compared to the previous close. Qingfa, Yongfu, Fuxing, Yongshang, and others bid up to 7.1 yuan. Huixiang sold heavily, causing the price to drop to 6.6 yuan. Fuxing, Yong, Huixiang, Chunyuan, Yong, Yingxiang, Yuanchang, Yong all bought, raising the price to 7 yuan. Fuxing, Yong, Huixiang, Xianghe, Qingfa, and Yong sold off at higher prices. The Shanghai branch of Banque Belge quoted the four-month U.S. dollar at 8.125, dropping to 6.5 yuan. Lack of Activity Among Chinese Merchants; the Foreign Exchange Market is Even More Calm; the Result is Both British and American Currencies Remain Flat 178
